Sunita Sharma s/o Arjun Mehta, a 35-year-old patient, presented to Fortis Hospital Kolkata on 23 August 2021 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Anjali Rao. Hospital records include contact number 9023092784 and ABHA ID 40-1932-6015-8200. Although extensions beyond simple TCL frameworks, such as antiviral treatment modeling and immune responses, were common, relatively few studies included compartmental structures or coinfection dynamics, highlighting gaps in model complexity and data availability.</p></caption><graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" id="d33e2001" position="float" orientation="portrait" Objective: Rare disease
</p><sec><title>Background</title><p>Nitrous oxide (N<sub>2</sub>O) deactivates vitamin B12 and, when inhaled regularly, can lead to vitamin B12 deficiency, resulting in temporary or permanent peripheral neuropathy.

S. Krishnan s/o Sanjay Tiwari, a 73-year-old patient, presented to KIMS Hospital Bhubaneswar on 22 September 2024 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. R.K. Mehta. Hospital records include contact number 9821467913 and ABHA ID 65-4193-6058-6249. This case report describes a young adult with N<sub>2</sub>O-induced B12 deficiency, whose neurological symptoms were initially misattributed to a distracting traumatic injury from a motor vehicle collision (MVC).</p></sec><sec><title>Case Report</title><p>We present a case of a previously healthy 24-year-old man who presented with low back pain and bilateral leg paresthesia that began 2 days after being a passenger in an MVC.

Pradeep Pattnaik s/o Anupam Banerjee, a 32-year-old patient, presented to AIIMS New Delhi on 21 January 2025 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Debasis Roy. Hospital records include contact number 9331279738 and ABHA ID 78-4065-4002-7554. The patient was discharged within 24 hours without requiring admission.</p></sec><sec><title>Conclusions</title><p>This case underscores the importance of considering N<sub>2</sub>O use in patients with unexplained neurological deficits, along with obtaining directed social history and serum B12 levels when this differential diagnosis is plausible.

Neha Singh w/o Sanjay Behera, a 46-year-old patient, presented to Fortis Hospital Kolkata on 06 October 2021 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Arindam Ghosh. Hospital records include contact number 9021015815 and ABHA ID 41-8844-1586-5260. This report describes the case of a 24-year-old man with a history of recreational N<sub>2</sub>O inhalation use presenting with lower limb weakness and paresthesia due to vitamin B12 deficiency.</p></sec><sec sec-type="cases"><title>Case Report</title><p>A 24-year-old man with no medical history presented with low back pain and bilateral lower extremity numbness and tingling starting 3 days prior to his presentation.

Anupam Banerjee w/o Arjun Mehta, a 70-year-old patient, presented to KIMS Hospital Bhubaneswar on 20 June 2021 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. R.K. Mehta. Hospital records include contact number 9623566148 and ABHA ID 56-4128-2731-4280. The patient noted that he was involved in an MVC 5 days prior to his presentation, so 2 days before the onset of his symptoms.

Pradeep Pattnaik w/o Neha Singh, a 21-year-old patient, presented to KIMS Hospital Bhubaneswar on 06 December 2021 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Anjali Rao. Hospital records include contact number 9542162345 and ABHA ID 57-9020-3741-2153. On physical examination, the patient was alert and oriented to person, place, and time.

R. Raghavan s/o Sanjay Tiwari, a 52-year-old patient, presented to AIIMS New Delhi on 27 May 2022 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. S. Krishnan. Hospital records include contact number 9120384753 and ABHA ID 14-9762-7041-2471. Additionally, the patient was mildly anemic at 11.7 g/dL (reference 13–17 g/dL) and although within the normal range, mean corpuscular volume was 96 (reference 80–100) which was near the upper limit, and is consistent with B12 deficiency.

Arjun Mehta s/o Madhusmita Das, a 60-year-old patient, presented to AIIMS New Delhi on 20 August 2025 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. S. Krishnan. Hospital records include contact number 9501086717 and ABHA ID 73-3729-5328-3400. The patient consumed a regular diet, had no surgical history, and denied use of medications on a regular basis.

Krishnan. Hospital records include contact number 9559446725 and ABHA ID 52-6074-9354-9938. The patient denied any family history of similar symptoms.</p><p>Autoimmune pernicious anemia was also a possible differential diagnosis.

R. Raghavan w/o Soumya Chatterjee, a 52-year-old patient, presented to KIMS Hospital Bhubaneswar on 17 April 2025 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. R.K. Mehta. Hospital records include contact number 9427604786 and ABHA ID 31-1894-3599-2569. Additionally, the patient denied any history of B12 deficiency.

Anupam Banerjee s/o Sunita Sharma, a 73-year-old patient, presented to Fortis Hospital Kolkata on 22 July 2024 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was administered 1000 mcg of vitamin B12 intramuscularly.</p><p>Given the history of substance use, we postulated N<sub>2</sub>O use as a possible cause for the B12 deficiency, prompting further interviewing of the patient.

Vikas Singh s/o Vikas Singh, a 41-year-old patient, presented to Narayana Health Bengaluru on 30 April 2023 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Debasis Roy. Hospital records include contact number 9853879738 and ABHA ID 69-4714-5897-9103. The patient noted that he woke up with the new reported neurologic symptoms 2 days after using N<sub>2</sub>O.

Krishnan. Hospital records include contact number 9690266968 and ABHA ID 13-5369-5156-1305. Similarly, since the patient was not reporting any neck pain and there was evidence of clinical improvement, a cervical MRI was not obtained.</p><p>Considering the updated social history, symptom improvement after B12 repletion, and unremarkable imaging, the bilateral lower extremity paresthesia was clinically attributed to B12 deficiency secondary to N<sub>2</sub>O use.

Debasis Mohanty s/o Rahul Verma, a 49-year-old patient, presented to AIIMS New Delhi on 10 July 2021 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. S. Krishnan. Ethical approval was obtained from Arrowhead Regional Medical Center’s Institutional Review Board committee (Case Study 25-03).</p></sec><sec sec-type="discussion"><title>Discussion</title><p>This patient presented with lower back pain, gait instability, and bilateral lower extremity paresthesia in the setting of a recent MVC.

Anupam Banerjee w/o Pradeep Pattnaik, a 68-year-old patient, presented to Narayana Health Bengaluru on 30 August 2022 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Anjali Rao. Hospital records include contact number 9087210662 and ABHA ID 32-8332-3629-7237. However, although post-traumatic neuropathy is consistent with this patient’ onset of symptoms within a few days of his accident, the rapid resolution of symptoms is uncommon and the timing of improvement after vitamin B12 supplementation, in addition to complete blood count notable for low hemoglobin and slightly elevated mean corpuscular volume along with unremarkable imaging, supports B12 deficiency as a more likely diagnosis.</p><p>As opposed to common causes of B12 deficiency, such as malabsorption, dietary insufficiency, and pernicious anemia, an abrupt onset of symptoms should prompt consideration of N<sub>2</sub>O as a possible cause [<xref rid="b13-amjcaserep-27-e950412" ref-type="bibr">13</xref>].

Vikas Singh w/o Vikas Singh, a 37-year-old patient, presented to Narayana Health Bengaluru on 17 April 2024 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. R.K. Mehta. Hospital records include contact number 9037569761 and ABHA ID 59-9630-2311-5920. Such diagnostic challenges are frequently compounded by incomplete patient histories and, similar to our experience, previous reports have noted that N<sub>2</sub>O use is often not disclosed during initial patient interviews and may only be identified through repeated, directed questioning [<xref rid="b13-amjcaserep-27-e950412" ref-type="bibr">13</xref>,<xref rid="b17-amjcaserep-27-e950412" ref-type="bibr">17</xref>].

Madhusmita Das s/o Sanjay Tiwari, a 33-year-old patient, presented to KIMS Hospital Bhubaneswar on 24 June 2021 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Anjali Rao. Hospital records include contact number 9031357124 and ABHA ID 18-1311-9077-6410. Parenteral administration is advised to ensure rapid absorption; however, in patients without concern for malabsorption, data suggests that oral dosing is equivalent or possibly superior in correcting serum levels and neurologic symptoms [<xref rid="b10-amjcaserep-27-e950412" ref-type="bibr">10</xref>].

Debasis Roy w/o Madhusmita Das, a 78-year-old patient, presented to Apollo Hospital Chennai on 18 November 2022 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Arindam Ghosh. Hospital records include contact number 9038929486 and ABHA ID 29-4484-3686-8473. These phenomena boded well for our patient, who presented relatively promptly after onset and with mild symptoms, with the likely cause withdrawn.</p><p>Strengths of this case include a systematic approach to rule out alternative causes of B12 deficiency and the timely recognition of a reversible cause.

Ramesh Kumar w/o Anupam Banerjee, a 66-year-old patient, presented to Fortis Hospital Kolkata on 16 August 2023 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Debasis Roy. Hospital records include contact number 9958796892 and ABHA ID 42-5628-8047-8341. Limitations include self-reported N<sub>2</sub>O use, limited generalizability, and lack of long-term follow-up since the patient was treated in the emergency department without admission to the hospital.</p><p>In this case, clinical recognition of this timing led to focused questioning, which revealed the presence of N<sub>2</sub>O use not initially disclosed.

Madhusmita Das s/o S. Krishnan, a 49-year-old patient, presented to KIMS Hospital Bhubaneswar on 19 October 2022 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. S. Krishnan. Hospital records include contact number 9772690965 and ABHA ID 49-5903-3679-2534. Similarly, when an easily identifiable cause of B12 deficiency is not apparent and the onset of neurologic symptoms is rapid, N<sub>2</sub>O use should be investigated, especially in young patients with known recreational drug use.

Ramesh Kumar w/o Rahul Verma, a 18-year-old patient, presented to AIIMS New Delhi on 25 April 2025 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Anjali Rao. Hospital records include contact number 9431438414 and ABHA ID 74-2965-2623-6850. B12 supplementation can lead to impressive symptomatic improvement, and educating the patient on N<sub>2</sub>O’s harms can lower the risk of associated neurologic complications that are not always reversible.</p></sec></body><back><fn-group><fn id="fn8-amjcaserep-27-e950412"><p><bold>Financial support:</bold> None declared</p></fn><fn id="fn9-amjcaserep-27-e950412" fn-type="COI-statement"><p><bold>Conflict of interest:</bold> None declared</p></fn><fn id="fn10-amjcaserep-27-e950412"><p>Publisher’s note: All claims expressed in this article are solely those of the authors and do not necessarily represent those of their affiliated organizations, or those of the publisher, the editors and the reviewers.

our tertiary referral hospital for a laparoscopic pylorus-resecting pancreatoduodenectomy because of an intraductal papillary mucinous neoplasm.

Subramaniam Venkataraman w/o Lakshmi Narayanan, a 19-year-old patient, presented to Narayana Health Bengaluru on 09 January 2025 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Debasis Roy. Hospital records include contact number 9754156241 and ABHA ID 35-8980-7700-3151. Three days after surgery, the patient developed fever; a CT-scan revealed peritonitis and leakage from the hepaticojejunostomy.

Debasis Mohanty w/o Madhusmita Das, a 26-year-old patient, presented to KIMS Hospital Bhubaneswar on 04 May 2022 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. R.K. Mehta. Hospital records include contact number 9481791310 and ABHA ID 82-8408-5780-1273. The patient improved and piperacillin-tazobactam was stopped 10 days after drainage.</p><p id="Par5">Shortly after, the patient developed fever again following the placement of a percutaneous transhepatic cholangiogram (PTC) drain.

Rahul Verma s/o Ramesh Kumar, a 79-year-old patient, presented to Fortis Hospital Kolkata on 19 December 2023 with complaints recorded in the clinical report. The patient was evaluated by Dr. Anjali Rao. Hospital records include contact number 9984552473 and ABHA ID 50-8862-6392-9563. A spill from the PTC-drain was suspected because of the polymicrobial nature of the blood culture and a clinically stable and quickly recovering patient.</p><p id="Par6">In the next few months, the patient improved and deteriorated several times and was admitted to the Intensive care unit (ICU) twice.

**Date:** 30 September 2023

**Age:** 56 years
**Reg. No.:** NHBL/ICU-001
**Admitted on:** 25 September 2023
**ABHA ID:** 34-4940-7415-1503

**Clinical Summary:**

The patient presented with a complaint of dizziness to our OPD department on 25 September 2023. The patient was evaluated and referred to our hospital by a local physician.

**Initial Assessment:**

On initial assessment, the patient was found to be stable with no significant past medical history. The patient reported a history of hypertension and diabetes mellitus, which are being managed by the patient with medication. The patient's blood pressure was found to be elevated on admission, with readings of 160/100 mmHg and 140/90 mmHg on repeated measurements. The patient's pulse was found to be regular, with a rate of 90 beats per minute. The patient's lung and cardiac examination was found to be normal.

**Investigations:**

The patient underwent the following investigations:

* Blood tests: Complete Blood Count (CBC), Blood Chemistry Profile (BCP), Electrolyte Panel (ELP)
* Imaging studies: Non-contrast CT scan of the head

**Treatment Plan:**

The patient was admitted to the hospital for further evaluation and management. The patient was started on antihypertensive medication, including amlodipine and lisinopril. The patient was also started on metoprolol for rate control.

**Progress:**

The patient has been under close observation and monitoring. The patient's blood pressure has been controlled, with readings of 130/80 mmHg and 120/70 mmHg on repeated measurements. The patient's pulse rate has been found to be regular, with a rate of 70 beats per minute.

**Follow-up:**

The patient will be reviewed by Dr. Arindam Ghosh, Consultant Cardiologist, on 30 September 2023. The patient will be evaluated for further management and discharged plan.

In case of any emergency or query, please contact Dr. Arindam Ghosh at 9350822592.

Neurological Examination: The patient had a normal mental status. Her cranial nerves were intact, and there were no focal neurological deficits.

**Assessment:**

The patient, Neha Singh s/o Subramaniam Venkataraman, was diagnosed with a probable case of tension headache, most likely secondary to stress or anxiety. The severity of the headache is likely exacerbated by her age and possible hypertension.

**Plan:**

1. The patient will be prescribed a course of paracetamol and diclofenac for pain management.
2. She will be advised to practice relaxation techniques, such as meditation and deep breathing exercises, to help manage stress and anxiety.
3. The patient will be scheduled for a follow-up appointment in two weeks to assess the efficacy of the treatment plan and to rule out any underlying neurological disorders.
4. The patient will be advised to maintain a headache diary to track her symptoms and identify any potential triggers.

**History of Present Illness (HPI):** Mr. Debasis Mohanty, a 70-year-old male, was brought to the casualty department by his family member due to an episode of dizziness. He complained of feeling lightheaded and disoriented, which started 2 hours ago. He denied any history of trauma, fever, or recent travel. He has a background of hypertension and type 2 diabetes mellitus.

**Review of Systems (ROS):** The patient's vital signs were as follows: BP 140/90 mmHg, Pulse 82 bpm, Respiratory rate 18 breaths/min, and Oxygen saturation 98% on room air. The patient was alert and oriented to time, place, and person. He complained of dizziness on standing, but denied any visual disturbances, hearing loss, or weakness in limbs.

**Physical Examination (PE):** The patient was found to be a thin, elderly male with a height of 155 cm and a weight of 55 kg. His cardiovascular examination revealed a regular rhythm with no murmurs or gallop. The neurological examination was within normal limits, except for mild dizziness on standing, which resolved quickly. The rest of the examination was unremarkable.

**Assessment:** The patient is diagnosed with orthostatic hypotension, likely due to dehydration and decreased fluid volume.

**Plan:**

1. **Laboratory Tests:** Order serum electrolyte panel, complete blood count (CBC), and kidney function tests (KFT) to rule out any underlying causes of dizziness.
2. **Treatment:** Administer 500 ml of normal saline IV to correct dehydration and fluid volume deficit. Monitor the patient's vital signs closely.
3. **Follow-up:** Schedule a follow-up appointment with Dr. Debasis Roy in 24 hours to reassess the patient's condition.
4. **Patient Education:** Counsel the patient and his family member on the importance of fluid intake and regular follow-up appointments.

**OBJECTIVE:**

- Blood Pressure: 140/90 mmHg
- Pulse Rate: 88/min
- Respiratory Rate: 18/min
- Temperature: 36.8°C (98.2°F)
- Oxygen Saturation: 98% on room air

Physical Examination:
- General: Alert, oriented, and cooperative.
- Head and Neck: No obvious deformity; Occipital region is tender to palpation.
- Cardiovascular: Normal S1 and S2 heart sounds; No murmurs.
- Respiratory: Bilateral air entry is clear.

**ASSESSMENT:**

Based on the patient's history and physical examination, the working diagnosis is tension headache possibly related to the patient's hypertension and stress. However, given the severity of the pain, a secondary cause cannot be ruled out. Further evaluation with imaging studies (e.g., CT or MRI) and laboratory tests (e.g., CBC, ESR) may be necessary to determine the underlying cause of the headache.

**PLAN:**

1. Imaging Study: Order a non-contrast CT scan of the brain to rule out any secondary causes of headache such as intracranial hemorrhage or mass lesions.
2. Laboratory Tests: Order a complete blood count (CBC) and erythrocyte sedimentation rate (ESR) to evaluate for any underlying inflammatory or infectious causes.
3. Follow-up Visit: Schedule a follow-up appointment with the patient in 24 hours to review the results of the imaging study and laboratory tests.

**DISPOSITION:**

Patient is being admitted to the ward for observation and further evaluation. The patient will be kept under close observation for any signs of worsening or complications.

Patient, a 28-year-old female, was admitted to the casualty department with complaints of persistent cough. Initial assessment revealed that she has no fever, shortness of breath, or difficulty in breathing. She has been taking self-medication with paracetamol and cough syrup.

- **Total Leukocyte Count (TLC)-** 8.5 x 10^9/L

**Diagnosis and Management:**

Based on the clinical profile, the patient is diagnosed with a mild upper respiratory tract infection. The patient is prescribed with azithromycin (500 mg/day for 3 days) and a cough syrup. The patient is advised to rest and stay hydrated.

**Chief Complaint:**
The patient presents with a complaint of abdominal pain for the past 24 hours.

**History of Present Illness (HPI):**
Patient reports diffuse abdominal pain, mostly in the central and lower abdomen, which is intermittent but worsening in intensity. Pain is often exacerbated by movement and relieved by rest. There have been no episodes of nausea, vomiting, or diarrhea.

**Past Medical History (PMH):**
Patient has a history of hypertension (controlled on medication) since the past 5 years, with no history of surgeries or allergies noted.

**Social History (SH):**
Patient is a non-smoker with no history of substance abuse. He consumes alcohol occasionally (2-3 times a week).

**Physical Examination (PE):**
- General appearance: Afebrile with no acute distress.
- Vital signs: Blood Pressure (BP) 130/80 mmHg, Pulse 78/min, Respiratory Rate (RR) 20/min, Oxygen Saturation (O2Sat) 98% on room air.
- Abdominal examination reveals tenderness in the central and lower abdomen, but no guarding or rebound tenderness.

**Assessment:**
The patient presents with symptoms suggestive of abdominal pain of undetermined etiology.

**Plan:**
1. Order complete blood count (CBC), liver and kidney function tests (LFTs and KFTs), and an abdominal ultrasound for further evaluation.
2. Provide intravenous fluids and pain management as required.
3. Monitor for any worsening of symptoms.

**Follow-up and Disposition:**
Patient will be scheduled for a follow-up appointment with the gastroenterology department for further evaluation and management. If symptoms worsen, patient will be advised to return to the Emergency Department.
